The common beard trimmers are too big for precise trimming and the motor is not powerful enough to make trimming fast and painless. A major irritant for me is also the fact that most manufacturers do not offer combined corded\cordless operation on their less expensive models. You want to have the possibility to use your trimmer in corded mode for 2 reasons: First, with cordless-only trimmers, you will eventually forget to recharge it and be very frustrated if you have an important meeting or occasion that day ... Second, manufacturers intentionally put rechargeable batteries of average quality in cordless trimmers so that after a short while they will start losing charge fast and you will buy a new unit out of frustration. The Wahl pro Detailers are made to give professional results and stand years of daily abuse. They are small in size but they have a powerful rotary motor that makes trimming painless, quick and precise. They have a power cord so you will always be able to use them no matter what type of trimming you need to do. Honestly, I have used Wahl hair clippers since I was a kid and they are built to last and operate flawlessly if you clean them after usage and you oil the blades before each trimming. Coming with a wide blade exacerbates the problem. When I bought my first one it did not come with a wide blade even though it still cut into skin it didn't do it nearly as much and with enough use I could operate it in a manner without cutting skin. So if you're interested in buying this trimmer it would help to buy a blade less wide which wahl can supply. The other problem is that the bottom housing of the trimmer contains a HOOK which holds the spring that counteracts the force of the motor to make the blades move. This hook often breaks resulting in the trimmer losing power or failing if the hook is completely broken. I bought two of these clippers within 3 years with the same problem. So now I'm looking to buy a more reliable clipper and if you are looking to buy something more reliable I would suggest the and is T outliner. I used my uncle's to do a shape up lately, it was very precise with no cutting at all (to get cut with these you really have to try hard).   424. Solidly built. Love the fact it's not made in China. Love the 3 attachments; they're all short, so seek elsewhere if you want to leave your hair longer.<br /><br />I mostly bought this item for the corded plug. Batteries are a toxic poisonous mess in our waste stream. Rechargeable batteries CAN potentially make some sense to me, but only if they have a long life & you can eventually replace them. However, I'm not aware of a single rechargeable trimmer or haircutter on the market that allows you to open up the casing and replace the batteries.<br /><br />Here is my experience for my last 2 trimmers, both rechargeable Norelco's. Work adequately for up to 2 years, then they begin to progressively have greater difficulty holding a charge. By around its 3rd birthday you're having to leave it plugged into the wall all the time, otherwise the motor will drag. Eventually it barely operates even when plugged in. You can completely forget taking it with you anywhere, since once unplugged and in a suitcase for a few hours you have to plug it back in for 2 or more days to get the blades to BARELY move again. At that point you're either resigning yourself to using a weak instrument that is no longer even portable (I stubbornly did this for the last couple of years), or you're throwing the darn thing away, since the batteries cannot be removed/replaced.<br /><br />I finally had to give in and start shopping for a new trimmer when even a 10 second power outage would render my Norelco useless. I was grateful to find what I needed in this Wahl (corded, short trim lengths, good quality, good reviews, and USA made).<br /><br />I'm expecting the Wahl 8081 to last a lifetime, given the light use that I need it for (short mustache & goatee trimming twice/week), and the fact that I can travel with & and bang-around my ANCIENT corded Remington trimmer (which lacks adjustable cutting lengths, but still works!)
